5.5
Discussion
It is important to note that the obtained results with the model are prone to a significant uncertainty,
due to the lack of temperature data of depths larger than 1.2 m. The model results indicate a
thawed layer ranging from the surface to approximately 5 m below surface, which has not been
observed during the ERT or drilling. During the calibration, it was attempted to reduce the snow
cover, change the initial temperatures for the spin-up and change the soil characteristics in any way
possible. However, the final output in this type of model resulted every time in a significant thawed
soil layer close to the surface.
In any case, this model is definitely useful to compare different scenarios, and conclude which
192
==PAGE:218==
Chapter 5. Thermal modelling
adaptation measure will have the largest effect. This is also intended in this section, to assess the
effect of an embankment, thermosyphon, and to assess the change in thermal regime when no
measures are taken whatsoever.
It is clear that thermosyphons are the most effective way to stabilise the thermal regime both directly
after construction and by retrofitting the foundation. The embankment on the other hand, only
showed a significant beneficial effect on the thermal regime if it would have been constructed directly
after the construction of the mast. It has not been investigated however, how the thermal regime for
this case would be in the future.
Another conclusion is that the horizontal insulation does not seem to be operational anymore. This
malfunctioning of the design might have also caused the sudden deterioration of the thermal regime
and subsequently the stability of the mast. It is however unsure what the exact cause is of this issue,
and it could be useful for future designs to investigate further regarding this topic.
193
==PAGE:219==
Chapter 6
Summary and Conclusions
6.1
Summary
When engaging in civil engineering activities in the Arctic, it is important to consider the seasonal
frost and permafrost characteristics. The mechanical properties of frozen and thawed soil are
fundamentally different, and with the ongoing climate changes and the Arctic Amplification effect,
significant changes are likely to occur in the soil conditions in the Arctic in the near future.
This project shows clearly how sensitive the active layer is, as the severe settlements at the masts of
the power line must have occurred in a relatively short period of time due to a change in thermal
regime. This change in thermal regime caused consequently an alteration of the ground bearing
capacity, and it is therefore for the highest interest for Arctic communities that relevant research is
conducted. By providing answers and ensuring the safe operation of the critical infrastructure, the
local Arctic communities can thrive and experience further development of their living standards and
industrial opportunities.
In this project, there have been three general tasks conducted to reach the final goal of proposing the
most reliable adaptation method to stabilise the masts of the power line. The considered masts are
located along the south shore of the Second Fjord in Sisimiut and are constructed on sedimentary,
ice rich permafrost deposits.
The first task was the field work conducted at Mast 9 of the power line in the beginning of July
2022. During this field trip, all efforts were put on the collection of as much as possible useful data
and information regarding the site in general, the geotechnical specification and the thermal regime
of the subsurface around the mast. This has been achieved by successfully completing the following
activities.
Thanks to the drone footage, a detailed Digital Elevation Model (DEM), orthophoto and 3D model
were obtained by processing the drone images with the AgiSoft Metashape software. The combination
of the comprehensive way of controlling a drone, the small size of the drone and the easy-to-use Agisoft
software package, makes this methodology highly recommendable in future projects. Especially the
detailed DEM was extremely useful for the Electrical Resistivity Tomography (ERT) data processing
and inversion. The ERT measurements gave us a detailed look of the subsurface, with keeping
the governing uncertainties in mind. ERT profiles do not allow the user to determine exactly in
what absolute state the subsurface is, but the interpretation of such inverted profiles facilitate the
identification of sudden changes in the state of the soil. This enabled us to identify a clearly altered
soil volume directly around the mast, which is undoubtedly related with both the construction and
the presence of the mast. The natural soil conditions, i.e. the soil conditions at a distance far enough
from the mast, showed permafrost reaching at least 12 m below the surface level. The actual depth
of the lower boundary of the permafrost is probably much lower, but with the conducted surveying
the deeper soil layers possess to large uncertainties to draw conclusion from.
194
==PAGE:220==
Chapter 6. Summary and Conclusions
The collected frozen soil samples from the two boreholes showed a significant difference in ice content
in function of the distance to the mast. Samples form SIS2022-03, the borehole closest to the
mast, did not show a significant ice content in the first 1.5 m of the borehole, while samples from
SIS2022-04, the borehole furthest away from the mast, showed almost immediately significant ice
content. It is also very likely that there was a thawed layer present approximately 1 m below the
surface, at the location of borehole SIS2022-03. This thawed layer is possibly also observed by the
ERT data and was definitely not caused by saline pore water. In general, the effect of the mast has
been proven by investigating the ice content of the soil samples.
The general stratigraphy of the area is a peaty, highly organic layer closest to the surface, with
directly followed by a silty layer. Next, with increasing depth the silt content gradually decreases,
with at around 1.15 m below the surface a shift to lean clay soil types. Both boreholes showed a
similar stratigraphy.
The temperature measurements of the soil, air and mast foundation column provided us with
extremely useful data. Firstly, the soil temperatures showed the extent of the influence of the mast
on the surrounding soil layers. The mast mainly influences the top layer of the soil, and the closer to
the mast, the larger the influence. The downhill sensors showed a larger influence compared to the
sensors placed parallel to the Fjord. This asymmetrical influence of the mast on the surrounding
subsurface was confirmed by the active layer probing around the mast as well. Furthermore, the
deeper soil layers were also influenced, but by a smaller extent. It was remarkable to observe a
significant cooling effect by the mast as well, which increases the seasonal amplitude of the soil
temperatures even more that enhances the effectiveness of the soil frost actions.
The monitoring of the mast temperatures showed the effect of the air and solar radiation on the mast
temperature. Furthermore, the measured air temperatures have been used to validate the scaled
ERA5 data, which were downscaled efficiently by using the TopoSCALE method.
The second task in this project, was the processing of the permafrost samples in the laboratories
of DTU. The determination of the general soil characteristics, such as the water content, organic
content, grain density, Atterberg limits and grain size distribution allowed a better insight in the
type of soil encountered on site. The PARIO measurements provided us with the cumulative grain
size distribution curve. The PARIO proved to be very practical and delivered nice and consequent
results. By combining the Atterberg limits and the grain size distribution, and by following the USCS
methodology, the final conclusion was that the upper soil layers are indeed organic and siltier, while
the lower soil layers are lean clays.
The unfrozen water content was successfully determined, by measuring the dielectric permittivity
with the HydraProbe sensor. The hysteretic behaviour of the unfrozen water content was measured
as well. The determination of the thermal properties of the soil samples with the Specific Heat
sensors resulted in reasonable results. However, the verification of the results by using glass beads
showed some discrepancies between the measured thermal properties of the glass beads, and the
reported values by the manufacturer. Therefore, a study was performed to investigate if after all
the correct model is used that links the bulk thermal conductivity with the thermal conductivities of
the constituents of the measured multi-phase material. It was discovered that the commonly used
geometrical mean model is not the ideal model, and that the De Vries formulation could be more
accurate. This should be definitely further investigated to improve the current method to determine
thermal characteristics with the Specific Heat sensor.
The last task in this project, was the configuration and calibration of a thermal model in the
GeoStudio TEMP/W software. The soil temperature measurements were used for the calibration, in
combination with the observed stratigraphy thanks to the soil samples and the ERT measurements.
The climatological variables were provided by the scaled ERA5 data with TopoSCALE for the historical
modelling, and the future climate scenarios were based on trends of the CMIP5 RCP climate scenarios.
Two adaptation methods were modelled as well, more specifically the installation of thermosyphons
195
==PAGE:221==
Chapter 6. Summary and Conclusions
and the construction of a gravel embankment around the mast.
Firstly, the clear deviating soil characteristics between soil close to the mast, and soil further away from
the mast, i.e. natural soil, was proven by the modelling as well. The construction of an embankment
simultaneously with the construction of the mast could have kept the subsurface cool enough up
to today, but a thermosyphon would have been more effective such that a larger safety factor in
the latter case would have been achieved. Lastly, the model showed that the placed horizontal
insulation is not effective anymore, which is in line with the observations during the field work. For
the future scenarios, the model indicates that without any measures the soil would continue to warm
up, endangering the stability of the mast even more. If an embankment would be constructed for
instance this summer, the model predicts that the embankment does not have a sufficiently large
cooling capacity. It seems based on the model that eight thermosyphons would be effective enough
to stabilise the thermal regime, with a sufficiently large safety factor for the future.
6.2
Conclusions
The cause of the sudden settlements is very likely the change in the thermal regime directly around
the mast foundation, which caused the ice to melt, such that severe settlements could occur due
to the significant ice content of the natural soil. Furthermore, as the process was identified as a
self-reinforcing process, the change in thermal regime, ice content and the subsequent settlements
will become more significant as the time passes. This is probably the reason that in the first 10 years
after the construction no problems have been observed, and that suddenly in three years’ time the
settlements became worrying.
In order to stabilise the thermal regime around the mast foundation, the simple thermal model that
was configurated for this project, shows that in order to ensure the safe and reliable operation of the
power line, which is considered as a critically important infrastructure for Sisimiut, the construction
of eight thermosyphons should be taken into consideration. The construction of an embankment
at the current state of the thermal regime of the soil around the mast, proved to be an insufficient
measure. Note that the eventual number and type of thermosyphons should be decided after more
detailed modelling of the situation, due to the simplicity of the presented 2D axisymmetric model in
this project.
6.3
Recommendations for further work
Firstly, as the maximal depth of soil temperature measurements in this project is limited to 1.2 m,
it is highly recommended in future research and projects to construct a sensor set-up that reaches
much larger depths on the south shore of the Second Fjord to monitor the soil temperature. The
depth to bedrock and the detailed stratigraphy of the sedimentary permafrost deposits is also not
exactly known yet. These three mentioned issues could be solved by drilling one borehole until the
bedrock is reached and instrument it completely with temperature sensors.
Regarding the issues with the horizontal insulation, it would be worth considering what the exact cause
is for the failure, to ensure that in future projects such errors in the design or construction process
do not occur. A final objective for optimising the general design of power line masts, constructed
onto sedimentary, ice rich permafrost, is to configure a design guide, which couples the extent of
required adaptation against changing climate as a function of the governing or expected thawing and
freezing indices.
During the lab work, the measuring method with the Specific Heat sensor was used to determine the
thermal properties of the soil. However, as the verification measurements with glass beads did not
yield in the reported values by the manufacturer, further research should be conducted to optimise
196
==PAGE:222==
Chapter 6. Summary and Conclusions
this measuring technique. In this thesis, it has already been investigated what effect the used model
that links the thermal properties of the constituents of the medium with the bulk thermal property
has on the eventual result. It is clear that the geometrical mean model does not provide the most
accurate representation of reality and therefore other formulations should be considered such as the
De Vries method. Instead of verifying the method with silts and clays, sandy soils would also be
better to use as their grain characteristics are closer to the characteristics of glass beads.
Regarding the thermal modelling of the site, it is recommended in future work to use a 3D model
instead of 2D thermal model, due to the asymmetric alteration of the thermal regime around the
mast. Furthermore, in a 3D model, the slope could be represented in a more accurate way. As
during the field trip significant surface and ground water flows were observed, and due to the high ice
content of the soil, a coupling of the thermal model with a hydrological model would be definitely a
more realistic representation of reality. Therefore, soil investigations for determining the hydrological
characteristics of the soil at the Second Fjord should be conducted as well.
Lastly, as the air-, mast foundation-, and soil temperatures are monitored for at least 3 years more
from the date of the submission of this Thesis, it is highly recommended to process the longer time
series of the data and assess the changes in thermal regime followed by some adaptation measures
planned to be executed in the summer of 2023.

==PAGE:249==
Appendix A. Complementary data and information
A.7
Geological information
 
 
 
 
 
 
Notat 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Til: 
Peter Villumsen, Nukissiorfiit 
Fra: 
Karsten Pedersen 
Emne: 
Geologiske forhold, Tasersuaq, Sisimiut. 
Dato: 
09-maj-2006 
 
 
Geologiske forhold, Tasersuaq, Sisimiut. 
 
Fjeldgeologi: 
Tasersuaq-området er en del af det Nagssugtoqidiske foldebælte der strækker sig fra 
området omkring Tasiilaq i Østgrønland til Sisimiut-området i Vestgrønland. Foldebæltet 
består primært af metamorfiserede granitter og gnejser med indlejrede, omdannede 
sedimenter af arkæisk alder (4,0 – 2,5 mia. år) samt vulkanske bjergarter. 
Grundfjeldet i Tasersuaq-området består primært af gnejs med en alder påca. 1,79 – 1,65 
mia. år. 
 
Fjeldet i den vestlige del af Tasersuaq består af overordnet af granodioritsk til kvartsdioritisk 
gnejs. Området omkring indtags- og afløbsområdet består af gnejs med en syenitisk til 
monzonitisk sammensætning. Disse bjergarter har generelt et lavt indhold af kvarts og et højt 
indhold af feldspat. Dette område bliver gennemskåret af enkelte dykes af basaltisk 
sammensætning. Under ca. kote 400 m er fjeldet generelt overfladeforvitret og rustfarvet 
mens det ovenfor er mere upåvirket. Tykkelsen af den forvitrede del kan være op til 20 m. 
 
Bjergarterne har en generel foliation i en øst-vestlig retning. Sprækkeoptælling på borekerner 
viser at fjeldkvaliteten er ligger inden for området RQD = 49 (dårlig) til 95 (god). Der kan 
observeres svaghedszoner parallelt med foliationsretningen. Ved en boring er der påtruffet 
grundvand i kote ca. 7,5 m. 
 
Sedimentgeologi: 
Siden afsmeltningen fra seneste istid er der foregået en landhævning i området. I dag findes 
den øvre grænse for kvartære marine aflejringer i området i ca. kote 120 m. Generelt findes 
der mange uraflejringer (blokmarker) i dalsænkninger og på fjeldskråninger. 
 
I området ved Anden Fjorden overlejres fjeldet generelt af velsorterede til velgraderede 
smeltevandsmaterialer i sand-grusfraktionen. Der kan observeres smeltevandsterrasser 
inderst i Anden Fjorden i elvområdet. Grænsen mellem marine og fluviale aflejringer er 
ukendt. 
 
Der er observeret sedimenttykkelser på mellem 0 m og ca. 16 m i elvlejet mellem Tasersuaq 
og Anden Fjorden. Der er påtruffet frost i jorden fra ca. 0,5 m u.t. til ca. 6 m u.t. i juni måned. 
 
224

Appendix A. Complementary data and information
A.9
Coefficient values for interpolation function of per-
mittivity of pure water
Table A.3: Best fit parameters of the interpolation function for the dielectric permittivity based on
the work of Ellison [27].
Parameters for the three relaxations terms
